Hey Josh,

Nothing you’ve done wrong, just wanted to give you a heads up to please be
cautious on the back porch (particularly near the stairs) and don’t have
large groups of people out there (or really hang out there at all, which
hopefully isn’t too much of an inconvenience given it’s about to be winter).

The upstairs neighbors had a pretty large party a while ago and it’s caused
the porch to start tilting, as I imagine you’ve noticed. I’m looking at
options for having it fixed or replaced, but likely won’t be for a few
weeks at least, if not until early spring.

Just wanted to give you notice on this and as much info on timeline for a
fix as soon as possible. Let me know if you have any questions or other
issues!

Hey Josh,


Thanks for taking the time to send this over and for flagging
everything/providing photos. Unfortunately, the apartment was on the market
for a while, so things like the window and wall crack may have appeared
during that period (which is frustrating for me as well that Amanda didn’t
flag). Please do let me know if you find any others so we can take care of
them as quickly as possible.


*Parking:* I’ve asked the upstairs tenants to use the far right and far
left columns from now on, and to leave the middle open for you. They likely
won’t move their cars until tomorrow (or when they’re back in town if
traveling), but this should resolve the parking issue going forward.


*Urgent Repairs:* I’m unfortunately now out of town so some of these may be
a bit slower than normal to be completed. I’ll have a handyman come by in
the coming week or so to take care of the kitchen window, patio light, wall
crack, and broken vent. Once scheduled, I’ll confirm the date and time with
you.
Can you please confirm so I can order replacements:

   1. A measurement of the broken window, and
   2. Any information printed on the patio light bulb (particularly
   size/wattage/etc) and include a picture if possible


*Blinds:* Those were installed by the previous tenant — I had left them up
assuming they worked. This is a bit beyond what I’d normally agree to
repair apart from having it removed, but given other issues I’ll have the
handyman take down the blinds and install a curtain rod.


*Washer/Dryer:* thanks for flagging. I’ll apply a $50 rent reduction next
month so you can have a cleaner give them a proper deep clean.


*Walls & Carpets:* Two cleanings were done between the previous tenant
moving out in August (including a carpet shampoo, although by a general
cleaner not a carpet cleaning specialist), and several walls were repainted
or touched up. However, in general, the apartment was rented *as-is* in
terms of aesthetics, which also means none of the items you raised would be
charged to your deposit on move-out. Rent and security deposit were priced
roughly 20% lower than the prior tenant’s rent to reflect this (although
significant updates were made to the dishwasher, water heater, etc). That
said, I prefer to make improvements and fix things where possible, so when
the handyman is there for the other repairs, I’ll have him spend an hour or
two touching up a few of the more notable wall areas (if you want to
identify which those are based on your furniture/decor, etc.), and at least
get estimates for larger painting. I’ll also apply another $50 rent
reduction next month toward additional carpet cleaning (or however you’d
like to use it). I likely won’t look at deep cleaning or replacing/removing
carpet for wood flooring in the near future, but if you plan to rent the
apartment for multiple years, we can discuss more significant improvements
such as a full repainting or reflooring down the line.


So, in summary, please make payment of *$1,900 instead of $2,000* next week
for November rent, I’ll be in touch once the handyman is scheduled for
repairs, and let me know if there’s anything else you find.


Best,
Matthew

as possible.

far left columns and to leave the middle open for you. They likely won’t
move their cars until tomorrow (or when they’re back in town if traveling),
but this should resolve the parking issue going forward.


*Urgent Repairs:* I’m unforuntatley out of town so some of these may be a
bit slower than normal to be completed. I’ll have a handyman come by in the
coming week or so to take care of the kitchen window, patio light, wall
crack, and broken vent. Once scheduled, I’ll confirm the date and time with
you.
Can you please confirm so I can order replacements:

   1. The approximate measurement of the broken window, and
   2. Take of photo of the patio light bulb (particularly size/wattage/etc)


*Blinds:* Those were installed by the previous tenant — I had left them up
assuming they worked, but can have the handyman take them down if that
would be preferable.


*Washer/Dryer & Cleaning:* I understand the frustration there — I’ll apply
a $50 rent reduction next month so you can have a cleaner give them a
proper deep clean.


*Walls & Carpets:* Two cleanings were done between the previous tenant
moving out (including a carpet shampoo), and several walls were repainted
or touched up. However, in general, the apartment was rented *as-is* in
terms of aesthetics, which also means none of the items you raised would be
charged to your deposit on move-out. Rent and security deposit were priced
roughly 20% lower than the prior tenant’s rent to reflect this. That said,
I prefer to make improvements and fix things where possible, so when the
handyman is there for the other repairs, I’ll have him spend an hour or two
touching up a few of the more notable wall areas (if you want to identify
which those are based on your furniture/decor, etc.).


I’ll also apply another $50 rent reduction next month toward additional
carpet cleaning (or however you’d like to use it). I likely won’t look at
deep cleaning or replacing/removing carpet for wood flooring in the near
future, but if you plan to rent the apartment for multiple years, we can
discuss more significant improvements such as a full repainting or
recarpeting down the line. As mentioned — and as Amanda should have
communicated — the apartment was rented *as-is* aesthetically, and quite a
bit of money has already been put into updates like the dishwasher, water
heater, etc.


So, in summary, please make payment of *$1,900 instead of $2,000* next
week, I’ll be in touch once the handyman is scheduled for repairs, and let
me know if there’s anything else.


Best,
Matthew

Hey Josh,

Hope all is going well with your move in. Just wanted to send along a few
notes to ensure you get settled smoothly:


   -

   Parking: The far-left spots (when facing the house/Trumbull from the
   alley) in the back of the house are yours. You can probably fit two cars.
   Street parking is free as well. Let me know if you want to rent the middle
   spots in the back, or if someone blocks you in/out.
   -

   Electric: Please activate your DTE Energy account ASAP, with Oct 15 as
   your start date. They usually give a 1-month grace period, but service will
   likely lapse after October if not set up.
   -

   Trash/Recycling: Pickup is on Fridays. Please bring the bins in and out
   when you can. The current trash bins have a few small holes — I’ve ordered
   new ones.
   -

   Rent: You can send via Zelle to either my phone (404-312-6583) or email (
   matteisn@gmail.com). Direct bank transfer works too if you’d prefer —
   just ask for my info. Please pay before the 1st each month; late fees start
   after 4 days.
   -

   Lock Code: The new front door code is 6158.
   -

   Contact: Text/call for anything urgent. Email is best for non-urgent
   stuff.
   -

   FYI: I’ll be out of town Oct 20–30, so replies might be slower, but I’ll
   still be reachable.


Also — last tenant was pretty low-maintenance, but if there’s anything that
could make the place better or any issues pop up, please let me know. I’ve
got a few improvements in progress already.


Let me know if there’s anything else I can help with or you encounter any
issues!


Best,

Matthew

---------- Forwarded message ---------
From: Gabe O'Leary <oleary.gabe@gmail.com>
Date: Sun, Oct 12, 2025 at 18:00
Subject: Suggestions for after Seattle
To: Matt Eisner <matteisn@gmail.com>


Yo! Stoked to see yah.

This is what I would do if I were you (coastal vibe):

- Rent a car
- Checkout Mount Erie <https://maps.app.goo.gl/S4pjYY8KoaHqWjss9> (~ 2
hours) - you can hike or drive to the top of - cool views out across the
puget sound
- Check out Deception pass state park
<https://maps.app.goo.gl/YtjM7Hqo5grnQMzr9> - wander around trails
- Check out Oak Harbor/Coveland/Coupeville
- Eat dinner at Oystercatcher <https://maps.app.goo.gl/WH4Ha7nogMtTCxut8> -
had a delicious meal (tasting menu) here earlier this year.
- Stay on Whidbey for a night (Anchorage Inn
<https://maps.app.goo.gl/bWWShUZvPmfo3zcc7> or Captain Whidbey
<https://maps.app.goo.gl/taZNcMTC4NxnuiHm8>)
- Drive south to Keystone (Coupeville) ferry landing- Schedule here
<https://wsdot.com/ferries/schedule/scheduledetailbyroute.aspx?route=pt-key>.
You'll want to arrive 40 minutes to an hour early to ensure you get on
- Take ferry to Port Townsend
- Stay in Port Townsend - "Rainshadow of the Olympics" means it's more
likely to be dry even when it's raining in the rest of washington. That
said, it still may very well be wet.
- Eat Khu Larb <https://maps.app.goo.gl/Lww7mtG4Gqitdwc87> - bomb thai
restaurant
- Check out more trails in the area, or Port Angeles


Dunno how many days you have. You could spend a couple nights in Port
Townsend or continue around the Olympic peninsula if you want (Port
Angeles, Forks etc.)


Alternatively if you want more of a mountain vibe you could head to
Leavenworth, but many of the trails are starting to get snow. That said,
because Leavenworth is on the east side of the crest of the cascades it can
be drier/sunnier than the west side.

Could be worth booking something cancelable and making a game time decision
based on the weather. It's not busy season here so you can probably make
bookings at the last minute.

I also have this google maps list with a bunch of Bed & Breakfasts around
the state <https://maps.app.goo.gl/JVSEpZhuvbacR71LA> if you want to look
into more options.

Happy to answer any questions yah have, just text me!

---

Hi Leah,

To answer your questions from earlier:

   - Parking: Each unit has 1 row with 2 medium sized parking spots in
   them. It is possible to rent an additional row for $60 per month
   - Dog: dogs, cats, and other pets are generally okay with prior
   approval. There would be an additional fee of $50-100 per month depending
   on the size, etc. Can you tell us more about your roommate’s dog/provide a
   recent picture?
   - Cleaning and Maintenance: a deep cleaning is scheduled for 2 July, the
   day after the current tenant's lease formally ends and they finish moving
   out. We also are planning to do some light repainting, fixing of blinds,
   and any other necessary repairs when we do our final walkthrough on July 1.


We did have a few additional questions:

   - Can you tell us more about your roommates? Are they people you know?
   What year students are they? Can they prove income or have a
   co-signer/guarantor?
   - If you could each provide your full name, a LinkedIn link (or any
   public and verifiable profiles so that we potentially can avoid conducting
   formal background and credit checks), and any other info, that would be
   helpful to ensure we can move quickly if you'd like to move forward


Please do let us know what your timelines are/if you'd like to move
forward. We do have quite a bit of interest in the unit, but would prefer
to get in good tenants that are a fit with us and the occupants in the
upstairs unit (who are very fun/nice/smart). That being said, do try and
get back to us quickly so we can give you the best chance of getting the
unit if you'd like it.

Best

Hi Brian,


I’m getting my various docs and info together for my 2024 tax filing, and
had a couple of questions (sorry for the lengthy email, but I've
highlighted the urgent points).



4727 Trumbull purchase: The two somewhat time sensitive/“unknown” points to
me are related to the 3 unit residential property (one of the units I have
been living/working in) that I purchased in Detroit in Summer 2024, which
I’ll refer to as 4727 Trumbull. To provide some basic background info:


   - I had to purchase this/set up mortgage, title, insurance, etc through
   Vang Advisory LLC, as I was blocked at the last minute in closing from
   taking out a personal mortgage due to lack of 12 month rental history and
   was not able to set up a new LLC in time for close.
   - I set up a Delaware LLC to manage this (D4727 LLC via LegalZoom) a
   month or so later, which I intend to transfer the title, mortgage,
   insurance, and all other operations/billing this year (not immediately
   urgent, but as I get things together/plan for the future, is there anything
   taxable/etc I should consider around this transfer, or info I’ll need for
   the 2024 filing? I’ve run a handful of relevant transactions through this
   entity/its Mercury Bank account, but most has been via my personal Chase or
   VA LLC. I generally did a poor job segregating 4727 cash flows from other
   accounts, but do have a log of all relevant transactions in a spreadsheet.
   I do have some invoices/receipts, especially for larger transactions. Is
   there anything in particular I should be looking to include here for you? I
   hope to have this much more cleaned up when I can get everything running
   through D4272 LLC this year).



D4727 LLC annual filings:


   - For the Delaware company D4727 LLC, I set this up with LegalZoom, they
   are saying state filings are due imminently, and asking for $300+ to
   perform them.
   - Do you handle these state filings for this and Vang Advisory LLC as
   part of the federal filings, or do I need to do anything here? I do have a
   bank account for the entity via Mercury which I have used very little, but
   am planning to include a balance statement for filings. *SOMEWHAT URGENT
   QUESTION*: Should I go ahead with the LegalZoom filing service? Do you
   know if there is a way to file an extension, as I don’t have the info I
   imagine I need for the annual report for either currently?



Filing statement of operating a business in Michigan: I believe you had
mentioned I needed to file something stating the business around the 4727
property rental was operating in the state of Michigan? *SOMEWHAT URGENT
QUESTION*: Do I need to do this for both Vang Advisory LLC for the past
year or so, and/or D4727 LLC for going forward when I transfer the title
(or now)? Is there anything I need to do retroactively for the past year?



25th Street property:


   - In Summer 2023, I purchased a residential duplex in Detroit with a
   friend. I have a 30% stake and he has a 70% stake, but initially the
   title/insurance/mortgage was in my name. I believe all of these except
   maybe the mortgage have been transferred into a Michigan LLC (D25 LLC) as
   of January 2024
   - He has prepared a K1 statement for me, but is there anything else I
   need around this purchase/operating this company/the title transfer?



Apart from that, I'm collecting various docs for UK companies, personal
investment accounts, a cash gift from my mother, employment, etc. I may
have a few questions as I collect these.

I'll also likely have a few non-2024 filing related questions for planning
next year/the future, but I'll save these for after this year's filing is
done.

Let me know if there's anything you need from me in the meantime, and if
you have insight on the two questions above.

Best,

Matthew
